Question: Straight to Hell was the first ever country music release to merit the Parental Advisory label of the Recording Industry Association of America. | Expected: supports | Answer:  The statement is false. While Straight to Hell, the third studio album by American musician Hank Williams III, did receive the Parental Advisory label, it was not the first country music release to do so. The Parental Advisory label has been used on various genres of music, including country, since its introduction in 1987. The label is placed on recordings that contain explicit content, such as strong language, violence, or sexual content, and is intended to alert parents of material potentially unsuitable for children. The Recording Industry Association of America (RIAA) and the British Phonographic Industry (BPI) both use the label, and it has been affixed to physical and digital recordings, as well as some video games featuring licensed music. | Token_usage: 2 | Took: 2.346365213394165 |Semintic search took 0.01444697380065918 seconds, TogetherAI took 1.953035831451416 seconds
